<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q18: What is V8? ☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q18-what-is-v8-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q18: What is V8? ☆☆" href="#q18-what-is-v8-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The V8 library provides Node.js with a JavaScript engine (a program that converts Javascript code into lower level or machine code that microprocessors can understand), which Node.js controls via the V8 C++ API. V8 is maintained by Google, for use in Chrome.</p>
<p dir="auto">The Chrome V8 engine :</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>The V8 engine is written in C++ and used in Chrome and Nodejs.</li>
<li>It implements ECMAScript as specified in ECMA-262.</li>
<li>The V8 engine can run standalone we can embed it with our own C++ program.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>nodejs.org</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q19: What is libuv? ☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q19-what-is-libuv-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q19: What is libuv? ☆☆" href="#q19-what-is-libuv-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>libuv</strong> is a C library that is used to abstract non-blocking I/O operations to a consistent interface across all supported platforms. It provides mechanisms to handle file system, DNS, network, child processes, pipes, signal handling, polling and streaming. It also includes a thread pool for offloading work for some things that can't be done asynchronously at the operating system level.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>nodejs.org</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q20: What is the difference between returning a callback and just calling a callback? ☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q20-what-is-the-difference-between-returning-a-callback-and-just-calling-a-callback-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q20: What is the difference between returning a callback and just calling a callback? ☆☆" href="#q20-what-is-the-difference-between-returning-a-callback-and-just-calling-a-callback-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-en">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-c">//some more lines of code; -  won't be executed</span>

<span class="pl-en">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-c">//some more lines of code; - will be executed</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto">Of course returning will help the context calling async function get the value returned by callback.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">do2</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">log</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">trace</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Execute function: do2'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'do2 callback param'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">do2Result</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">do2</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-s1">log</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">trace</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">`print <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">${</span><span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>`</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s">`return from callback(<span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">${</span><span class="pl-s1">param</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>)`</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span> <span class="pl-c">// we could use that return</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-s1">log</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">trace</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">`print <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">${</span><span class="pl-s1">do2Result</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>`</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto">Output:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell" dir="auto"><pre>C:<span class="pl-cce">\W</span>ork<span class="pl-cce">\N</span>ode<span class="pl-k">&gt;</span>node --use-strict main.js
[0] Execute function: do2
[0] print do2 callback param
[0] print <span class="pl-k">return</span> from callback(do2 callback param)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q21: What is REPL in context of Node? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q21-what-is-repl-in-context-of-node-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q21: What is REPL in context of Node? ☆☆☆" href="#q21-what-is-repl-in-context-of-node-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>REPL</strong> stands for Read Eval Print Loop and it represents a computer environment like a window console or unix/linux shell where a command is entered and system responds with an output. Node.js or Node comes bundled with a REPL environment. It performs the following desired tasks.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Read</strong> - Reads user's input, parse the input into JavaScript data-structure and stores in memory.</li>
<li><strong>Eval</strong> - Takes and evaluates the data structure</li>
<li><strong>Print</strong> - Prints the result</li>
<li><strong>Loop</strong> - Loops the above command until user press ctrl-c twice.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q22: What is Callback? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q22-what-is-callback-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q22: What is Callback? ☆☆☆" href="#q22-what-is-callback-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Callback</strong> is an asynchronous equivalent for a function. A callback function is called at the completion of a given task. Node makes heavy use of callbacks. All APIs of Node are written is such a way that they supports callbacks.</p>
<p dir="auto">For example, a function to read a file may start reading file and return the control to execution environment immediately so that next instruction can be executed. Once file I/O is complete, it will call the callback function while passing the callback function, the content of the file as parameter. So there is no blocking or wait for File I/O.</p>
<p dir="auto">This makes Node.js highly scalable, as it can process high number of request without waiting for any function to return result.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q23: What is a blocking code? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q23-what-is-a-blocking-code-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q23: What is a blocking code? ☆☆☆" href="#q23-what-is-a-blocking-code-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
If application has to wait for some I/O operation in order to complete its execution any further then the code responsible for waiting is known as blocking code.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q24: How Node prevents blocking code? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q24-how-node-prevents-blocking-code-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q24: How Node prevents blocking code? ☆☆☆" href="#q24-how-node-prevents-blocking-code-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
By providing callback function. Callback function gets called whenever corresponding event triggered.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q25: What is Event Loop? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q25-what-is-event-loop-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q25: What is Event Loop? ☆☆☆" href="#q25-what-is-event-loop-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Node.js is a single threaded application but it support concurrency via concept of event and callbacks. As every API of Node js are asynchronous and being a single thread, it uses async function calls to maintain the concurrency. Node uses observer pattern. Node thread keeps an event loop and whenever any task get completed, it fires the corresponding event which signals the event listener function to get executed.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q26: What is Event Emmitter? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q26-what-is-event-emmitter-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q26: What is Event Emmitter? ☆☆☆" href="#q26-what-is-event-emmitter-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
All objects that emit events are members of EventEmitter class. These objects expose an <code>eventEmitter.on()</code> function that allows one or more functions to be attached to named events emitted by the object.</p>
<p dir="auto">When the EventEmitter object emits an event, all of the functions attached to that specific event are called synchronously.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-v">EventEmitter</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'events'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">MyEmitter</span> <span class="pl-k">extends</span> <span class="pl-v">EventEmitter</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">myEmitter</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">MyEmitter</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">myEmitter</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">on</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'event'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'an event occurred!'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">myEmitter</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">emit</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'event'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q27: What is purpose of Buffer class in Node? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q27-what-is-purpose-of-buffer-class-in-node-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q27: What is purpose of Buffer class in Node? ☆☆☆" href="#q27-what-is-purpose-of-buffer-class-in-node-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Buffer</strong> class is a global class and can be accessed in application without importing buffer module. A Buffer is a kind of an array of integers and corresponds to a raw memory allocation outside the V8 heap. A Buffer cannot be resized.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q28: What is difference between synchronous and asynchronous method of fs module? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q28-what-is-difference-between-synchronous-and-asynchronous-method-of-fs-module-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q28: What is difference between synchronous and asynchronous method of fs module? ☆☆☆" href="#q28-what-is-difference-between-synchronous-and-asynchronous-method-of-fs-module-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">Every method in <code>fs</code> module has synchronous as well as asynchronous form. Asynchronous methods takes a last parameter as completion function callback and first parameter of the callback function is error. It is preferred to use asynchronous method instead of synchronous method as former never block the program execution where the latter one does.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q29: What are streams? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q29-what-are-streams-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q29: What are streams? ☆☆☆" href="#q29-what-are-streams-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Streams are objects that let you read data from a source or write data to a destination in continuous fashion. In Node.js, there are four types of streams.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Readable</strong> - Stream which is used for read operation.</li>
<li><strong>Writable</strong> - Stream which is used for write operation.</li>
<li><strong>Duplex</strong> - Stream which can be used for both read and write operation.</li>
<li><strong>Transform</strong> - A type of duplex stream where the output is computed based on input.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q30: What is Chaining in Node? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q30-what-is-chaining-in-node-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q30: What is Chaining in Node? ☆☆☆" href="#q30-what-is-chaining-in-node-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Chanining</strong> is a mechanism to connect output of one stream to another stream and create a chain of multiple stream operations. It is normally used with piping operations.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q31: What is the purpose of setTimeout function? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q31-what-is-the-purpose-of-settimeout-function-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q31: What is the purpose of setTimeout function? ☆☆☆" href="#q31-what-is-the-purpose-of-settimeout-function-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The <code>setTimeout(cb, ms)</code> global function is used to run callback <code>cb</code> after at least <code>ms</code> milliseconds. The actual delay depends on external factors like OS timer granularity and system load. A timer cannot span more than 24.8 days.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q32: How can you avoid callback hells? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q32-how-can-you-avoid-callback-hells-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q32: How can you avoid callback hells? ☆☆☆" href="#q32-how-can-you-avoid-callback-hells-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
To do so you have more options:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>modularization</strong>: break callbacks into independent functions</li>
<li>use <em>Promises</em></li>
<li>use <code>yield</code> with <em>Generators</em> and/or <em>Promises</em></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q33: What's the event loop? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q33-whats-the-event-loop-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q33: What's the event loop? ☆☆☆" href="#q33-whats-the-event-loop-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>The event loop</strong> is what allows Node.js to perform non-blocking I/O operations — despite the fact that JavaScript is single-threaded — by offloading operations to the system kernel whenever possible.</p>
<div dir="auto">
<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/37d093d946a3f156d97328a099f1e0954b971a24db4bd42c4566ae26f521a59e/68747470733a2f2f692e737461636b2e696d6775722e636f6d2f4c6273397a2e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/37d093d946a3f156d97328a099f1e0954b971a24db4bd42c4566ae26f521a59e/68747470733a2f2f692e737461636b2e696d6775722e636f6d2f4c6273397a2e706e67" data-canonical-src="https://i.stack.imgur.com/Lbs9z.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a>
</div>
<p dir="auto">Every I/O requires a callback - once they are done they are pushed onto the event loop for execution. Since most modern kernels are multi-threaded, they can handle multiple operations executing in the background. When one of these operations completes, the kernel tells Node.js so that the appropriate callback may be added to the poll queue to eventually be executed.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q34: How to avoid callback hell in Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q34-how-to-avoid-callback-hell-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q34: How to avoid callback hell in Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q34-how-to-avoid-callback-hell-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Node.js internally uses a single-threaded event loop to process queued events. But this approach may lead to blocking the entire process if there is a task running longer than expected.</p>
<p dir="auto">Node.js addresses this problem by incorporating callbacks also known as higher-order functions. So whenever a long-running process finishes its execution, it triggers the callback associated.</p>
<p dir="auto">sometimes, it could lead to complex and unreadable code. More the no. of callbacks, longer the chain of returning callbacks would be.</p>
<p dir="auto">There are four solutions which can address the callback hell problem.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Make your program modular</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">It proposes to split the logic into smaller modules. And then join them together from the main module to achieve the desired result.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Use async mechanism</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">It is a widely used Node.js module which provides a sequential flow of execution.</p>
<p dir="auto">The async module has &lt;async.waterfall&gt; API which passes data from one operation to other using the next callback.</p>
<p dir="auto">Another async API &lt;async.map&gt; allows iterating over a list of items in parallel and calls back with another list of results.</p>
<p dir="auto">With the async approach, the caller’s callback gets called only once. The caller here is the main method using the async module.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Use promises mechanism</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">Promises give an alternate way to write async code. They either return the result of execution or the error/exception. Implementing promises requires the use of &lt;.then()&gt; function which waits for the promise object to return. It takes two optional arguments, both functions. Depending on the state of the promise only one of them will get called. The first function call proceeds if the promise gets fulfilled. However, if the promise gets rejected, then the second function will get called.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Use generators</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">Generators are lightweight routines, they make a function wait and resume via the yield keyword. Generator functions uses a special syntax &lt;function* ()&gt;. They can also suspend and resume asynchronous operations using constructs such as promises or  and turn a synchronous code into asynchronous.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q35: Explain how does Node.js work? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q35-explain-how-does-nodejs-work-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q35: Explain how does Node.js work? ☆☆☆" href="#q35-explain-how-does-nodejs-work-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
A Node.js application creates a single thread on its invocation. Whenever Node.js receives a request, it first completes its processing before moving on to the next request.</p>
<p dir="auto">Node.js works asynchronously by using the event loop and callback functions, to handle multiple requests coming in parallel. An Event Loop is a functionality which handles and processes all your external events and just converts them to a callback function. It invokes all the event handlers at a proper time. Thus, lots of work is done on the back-end, while processing a single request, so that the new incoming request doesn’t have to wait if the processing is not complete.</p>
<div dir="auto">
<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer nofollow" href="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/df7e1642c392d007afbdf7dd54f453b24bef4cfca96c43f1df13e31be28a6eab/68747470733a2f2f637368617270636f726e65722d6d696e64637261636b6572696e632e6e6574646e612d73736c2e636f6d2f61727469636c652f6e6f64652d6a732d6576656e742d6c6f6f702f496d616765732f312e706e67"><img src="https://camo.githubusercontent.com/df7e1642c392d007afbdf7dd54f453b24bef4cfca96c43f1df13e31be28a6eab/68747470733a2f2f637368617270636f726e65722d6d696e64637261636b6572696e632e6e6574646e612d73736c2e636f6d2f61727469636c652f6e6f64652d6a732d6576656e742d6c6f6f702f496d616765732f312e706e67" data-canonical-src="https://csharpcorner-mindcrackerinc.netdna-ssl.com/article/node-js-event-loop/Images/1.png" style="max-width: 100%;"></a>
</div>
<p dir="auto">While processing a request, Node.js attaches a callback function to it and moves it to the back-end. Now, whenever its response is ready, an event is called which triggers the associated callback function to send this response.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q16: When should we use Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q16-when-should-we-use-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q16: When should we use Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q16-when-should-we-use-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Node.js</strong> is well suited for applications that have a lot of concurrent connections and each <em>request only needs very few CPU cycles</em>, because the event loop (with all the other clients) is blocked during execution of a function. I believe Node.js is best suited for real-time applications: online games, collaboration tools, chat rooms, or anything where what one user (or robot? or sensor?) does with the application needs to be seen by other users immediately, without a page refresh.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q17: How does Node.js handle child threads? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q17-how-does-nodejs-handle-child-threads-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q17: How does Node.js handle child threads? ☆☆☆" href="#q17-how-does-nodejs-handle-child-threads-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Node.js, in its essence, is a single thread process. It does not expose child threads and thread management methods to the developer. Technically, Node.js does spawn child threads for certain tasks such as asynchronous I/O, but these run behind the scenes and do not execute any application JavaScript code, nor block the main event loop.</p>
<p dir="auto">If threading support is desired in a Node.js application, there are tools available to enable it, such as the ChildProcess module.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>lazyquestion.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q18: What is the preferred method of resolving unhandled exceptions in Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q18-what-is-the-preferred-method-of-resolving-unhandled-exceptions-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q18: What is the preferred method of resolving unhandled exceptions in Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q18-what-is-the-preferred-method-of-resolving-unhandled-exceptions-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Unhandled exceptions in Node.js can be caught at the <code>Process</code> level by attaching a handler for <code>uncaughtException</code> event.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-s1">process</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">on</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'uncaughtException'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Caught exception: '</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">However, <code>uncaughtException</code> is a very crude mechanism for exception handling and may be removed from Node.js in the future. An exception that has bubbled all the way up to the <code>Process</code> level means that your application, and Node.js may be in an undefined state, and the only sensible approach would be to restart everything.</p>
<p dir="auto">The preferred way is to add another layer between your application and the Node.js process which is called the <a href="http://nodejs.org/api/domain.html" rel="nofollow">domain</a>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Domains provide a way to handle multiple different I/O operations as a single group. So, by having your application, or part of it, running in a separate domain, you can safely handle exceptions at the domain level, before they reach the <code>Process</code> level.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>lazyquestion.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q19: What is stream and what are types of streams available in Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q19-what-is-stream-and-what-are-types-of-streams-available-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q19: What is stream and what are types of streams available in Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q19-what-is-stream-and-what-are-types-of-streams-available-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Streams</strong> are a collection of data that might not be available all at once and don’t have to fit in memory. Streams provide chunks of data in a continuous manner. It is useful to read a large set of data and process it.</p>
<p dir="auto">There is four fundamental type of streams:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Readable.</li>
<li>Writeable.</li>
<li>Duplex.</li>
<li>Transform.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Readable streams as the name suggest used in reading a large chunk of data from a source. Writable streams are used in writing a large chunk of data to the destination.</p>
<p dir="auto">Duplex streams are both readable and writable ( Eg socket). Transform stream is the duplex stream which is used in modifying the data (eg zip creation).</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codeforgeek.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q20: What are the global objects of Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q20-what-are-the-global-objects-of-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q20: What are the global objects of Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q20-what-are-the-global-objects-of-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
These objects are available in all modules:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>process</strong> - The process object is a global that provides information about, and control over, the current Node.js process.</li>
<li><strong>console</strong> - Used to print to stdout and stderr.</li>
<li><strong>buffer</strong> - Used to handle binary data.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/jimuyouyou</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q1: What is Piping in Node? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q1-what-is-piping-in-node-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q1: What is Piping in Node? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q1-what-is-piping-in-node-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Piping</strong> is a mechanism to connect output of one stream to another stream. It is normally used to get data from one stream and to pass output of that stream to another stream. There is no limit on piping operations.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q2: Name some of the events fired by streams. ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q2-name-some-of-the-events-fired-by-streams-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q2: Name some of the events fired by streams. ☆☆☆☆" href="#q2-name-some-of-the-events-fired-by-streams-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Each type of Stream is an <strong>EventEmitter</strong> instance and throws several events at different instance of times. For example, some of the commonly used events are:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>data</strong> - This event is fired when there is data is available to read.</li>
<li><strong>end</strong> - This event is fired when there is no more data to read.</li>
<li><strong>error</strong> - This event is fired when there is any error receiving or writing data.</li>
<li><strong>finish</strong> - This event is fired when all data has been flushed to underlying system</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q3: What is the purpose of __filename variable? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q3-what-is-the-purpose-of-__filename-variable-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q3: What is the purpose of __filename variable? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q3-what-is-the-purpose-of-__filename-variable-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The <code>__filename</code> represents the filename of the code being executed. This is the resolved absolute path of this code file. For a main program this is not necessarily the same filename used in the command line. The value inside a module is the path to that module file.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q4: How can you listen on port 80 with Node? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q4-how-can-you-listen-on-port-80-with-node-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q4: How can you listen on port 80 with Node? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q4-how-can-you-listen-on-port-80-with-node-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Run the application on any port above 1024, then put a reverse proxy like <a href="http://nginx.org/" rel="nofollow">nginx</a> in front of it.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q5: What tools can be used to assure consistent code style? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q5-what-tools-can-be-used-to-assure-consistent-code-style-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q5: What tools can be used to assure consistent code style? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q5-what-tools-can-be-used-to-assure-consistent-code-style-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
You have plenty of options to do so:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="http://jslint.com/" rel="nofollow">JSLint</a> by Douglas Crockford</li>
<li><a href="http://jshint.com/" rel="nofollow">JSHint</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eslint.org/" rel="nofollow">ESLint</a></li>
<li><a href="http://jscs.info/" rel="nofollow">JSCS</a></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">These tools are really helpful when developing code in teams, to enforce a given style guide and to catch common errors using static analysis.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q6: What's a stub? Name a use case. ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q6-whats-a-stub-name-a-use-case-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q6: What's a stub? Name a use case. ☆☆☆☆" href="#q6-whats-a-stub-name-a-use-case-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Stubs</strong> are functions/programs that simulate the behaviours of components/modules. Stubs provide canned answers to function calls made during test cases. Also, you can assert on with what these stubs were called.</p>
<p dir="auto">A use-case can be a file read, when you do not want to read an actual file:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">fs</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'fs'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">readFileStub</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">sinon</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">stub</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">fs</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">'readFile'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">path</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">cb</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">cb</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">null</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">'filecontent'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-en">expect</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">readFileStub</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">to</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">be</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">called</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">readFileStub</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">restore</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q7: Does Node.js support multi-core platforms? And is it capable of utilizing all the cores? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q7-does-nodejs-support-multi-core-platforms-and-is-it-capable-of-utilizing-all-the-cores-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q7: Does Node.js support multi-core platforms? And is it capable of utilizing all the cores? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q7-does-nodejs-support-multi-core-platforms-and-is-it-capable-of-utilizing-all-the-cores-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes, Node.js would run on a multi-core system without any issue. But it is by default a single-threaded application, so it can’t completely utilize the multi-core system.</p>
<p dir="auto">However, Node.js can facilitate deployment on multi-core systems where it does use the additional hardware. It packages with a Cluster module which is capable of starting multiple Node.js worker processes that will share the same port.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q8: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q8-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q8: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q8-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes, it’s true that Node.js processes all requests on a single thread. But it’s just a part of the theory behind Node.js design. In fact, more than the single thread mechanism, it makes use of events and callbacks to handle a large no. of requests asynchronously.</p>
<p dir="auto">Moreover, Node.js has an optimized design which utilizes both JavaScript and C++ to guarantee maximum performance. JavaScript executes at the server-side by Google Chrome v8 engine. And the C++ lib UV library takes care of the non-sequential I/O via background workers.</p>
<p dir="auto">To explain it practically, let’s assume there are 100s of requests lined up in Node.js queue. As per design, the main thread of Node.js event loop will receive all of them and forwards to background workers for execution. Once the workers finish processing requests, the registered callbacks get notified on event loop thread to pass the result back to the user.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q9: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q9-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q9: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q9-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes, it’s true that Node.js processes all requests on a single thread. But it’s just a part of the theory behind Node.js design. In fact, more than the single thread mechanism, it makes use of events and callbacks to handle a large no. of requests asynchronously.</p>
<p dir="auto">Moreover, Node.js has an optimized design which utilizes both JavaScript and C++ to guarantee maximum performance. JavaScript executes at the server-side by Google Chrome v8 engine. And the C++ lib UV library takes care of the non-sequential I/O via background workers.</p>
<p dir="auto">To explain it practically, let’s assume there are 100s of requests lined up in Node.js queue. As per design, the main thread of Node.js event loop will receive all of them and forwards to background workers for execution. Once the workers finish processing requests, the registered callbacks get notified on event loop thread to pass the result back to the user.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q10: When to not use Node.js? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q10-when-to-not-use-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q10: When to not use Node.js? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q10-when-to-not-use-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
We can use Node.js for a variety of applications. But it is a single threaded framework, so we should not use it for cases where the application requires long processing time. If the server is doing some calculation, it won’t be able to process any other requests. Hence, Node.js is best when processing needs less dedicated CPU time.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q11: Why to use Buffers instead of binary strings to handle binary data ? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q11-why-to-use-buffers-instead-of-binary-strings-to-handle-binary-data--" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q11: Why to use Buffers instead of binary strings to handle binary data ? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q11-why-to-use-buffers-instead-of-binary-strings-to-handle-binary-data--"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Pure JavaScript does not able to handle straight binary data very well. Since Node.js servers have to deal with TCP streams for reading and writing of data, binary strings will become problematic to work with as it is very slow and has a tendency to break. That's why it is always advisable to use Buffers instead of binary strings to handle binary data.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codingdefined.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q12: How to use Buffer in Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q12-how-to-use-buffer-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q12: How to use Buffer in Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q12-how-to-use-buffer-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Buffer is used to process binary data, such as pictures, mp3, database files, etc. Buffer supports a variety of encoding and decoding, binary string conversion.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/jimuyouyou</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q13: When should I use EventEmitter? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q13-when-should-i-use-eventemitter-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q13: When should I use EventEmitter? ☆☆☆" href="#q13-when-should-i-use-eventemitter-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Whenever it makes sense for code to <em>subscribe</em> to something rather than get a callback from something. The typical use case would be that there's multiple blocks of code in your application that may need to do something when an event happens.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com/</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q14: How do you debug Node.js applications? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q14-how-do-you-debug-nodejs-applications-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q14: How do you debug Node.js applications? ☆☆☆" href="#q14-how-do-you-debug-nodejs-applications-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q15: Rewrite promise-based Node.js applications to Async/Await ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q15-rewrite-promise-based-nodejs-applications-to-asyncawait-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q15: Rewrite promise-based Node.js applications to Async/Await ☆☆☆" href="#q15-rewrite-promise-based-nodejs-applications-to-asyncawait-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Details:</strong>
Rewrite this code to Async/Await:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">asyncTask</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-en">functionA</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueA</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-en">functionB</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueA</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueB</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-en">functionC</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueB</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueC</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-en">functionD</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueC</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">catch</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">logger</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">async</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">asyncTask</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">try</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">valueA</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">functionA</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">valueB</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">functionB</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueA</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">valueC</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">functionC</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueB</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">functionD</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">valueC</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span> <span class="pl-k">catch</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-s1">logger</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q16: What is the relationship between Node.js and V8? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q16-what-is-the-relationship-between-nodejs-and-v8-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q16: What is the relationship between Node.js and V8? ☆☆☆" href="#q16-what-is-the-relationship-between-nodejs-and-v8-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
V8 is the Javascript engine inside of node.js that parses and runs your Javascript. The same V8 engine is used inside of Chrome to run javascript in the Chrome browser. Google open-sourced the V8 engine and the builders of node.js used it to run Javascript in node.js.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q17: What is N-API in Node.js? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q17-what-is-n-api-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q17: What is N-API in Node.js? ☆☆☆" href="#q17-what-is-n-api-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>N-API</strong> (pronounced N as in the letter, followed by API) is an API for building native Addons. It is independent from the underlying JavaScript runtime (ex V8) and is maintained as part of Node.js itself. This API will be Application Binary Interface (ABI) stable across versions of Node.js. It is intended to insulate Addons from changes in the underlying JavaScript engine and allow modules compiled for one version to run on later versions of Node.js without recompilation.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>medium.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q18: Explain the concept of Domain in Node.js ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q18-explain-the-concept-of-domain-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q18: Explain the concept of Domain in Node.js ☆☆☆" href="#q18-explain-the-concept-of-domain-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Domains provide a way to handle multiple different IO operations as a single group. If any of the event emitters or callbacks registered to a domain emit an <code>error</code> event, or throw an error, then the domain object will be notified, rather than losing the context of the error in the <code>process.on('uncaughtException')</code> handler, or causing the program to exit immediately with an error code.</p>
<p dir="auto">Domain error handlers are not a substitute for closing down a process when an error occurs. The safest way to respond to a thrown error is to shut down the process. In a normal web server, the better approach is to send an error response to the request that triggered the error, while letting the others finish in their normal time, and stop listening for new requests in that worker.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">domain</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'domain'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">d</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">domain</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">create</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-c">// Domain emits 'error' when it's given an unhandled error</span>
<span class="pl-s1">d</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">on</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'error'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">stack</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-c">// Our handler should deal with the error in an appropriate way</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// Enter this domain</span>
<span class="pl-s1">d</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">run</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-c">// If an un-handled error originates from here, process.domain will handle it</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">process</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">domain</span> <span class="pl-c1">===</span> <span class="pl-s1">d</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span> <span class="pl-c">// true</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-c">// domain has now exited. Any errors in code past this point will not be caught.</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>nodejs.org</em></p>
