<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q19: Are you familiar with differences between Node.js nodules and ES6 nodules? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q19-are-you-familiar-with-differences-between-nodejs-nodules-and-es6-nodules-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q19: Are you familiar with differences between Node.js nodules and ES6 nodules? ☆☆☆" href="#q19-are-you-familiar-with-differences-between-nodejs-nodules-and-es6-nodules-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The modules used in Node.js follow a module specification known as the <strong>CommonJS</strong> specification. The recent updates to the JavaScript programming language, in the form of ES6, specify changes to the language, adding things like new class syntax and a module system. This module system is different from Node.js modules. To import ES6 module, we'd use the ES6 <code>import</code> functionality.</p>
<p dir="auto">Now ES6 modules are incompatible with Node.js modules. This has to do with the way modules are loaded differently between the two formats. If you use a compiler like Babel, you can mix and match module formats.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q20: What are the use cases for the Node.js "vm" core module? ☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q20-what-are-the-use-cases-for-the-nodejs-vm-core-module-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q20: What are the use cases for the Node.js &quot;vm&quot; core module? ☆☆☆" href="#q20-what-are-the-use-cases-for-the-nodejs-vm-core-module-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
It can be used to safely execute a piece of code contained in a string or file. The execution is performed in a separate environment that by default has no access to the environment of the program that created it. Moreover, you can specify execution timeout and context-specific error handling.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>quora.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q1: What is Piping in Node? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q1-what-is-piping-in-node--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q1: What is Piping in Node? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q1-what-is-piping-in-node--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Piping</strong> is a mechanism to connect output of one stream to another stream. It is normally used to get data from one stream and to pass output of that stream to another stream. There is no limit on piping operations.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q2: Name some of the events fired by streams. ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q2-name-some-of-the-events-fired-by-streams--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q2: Name some of the events fired by streams. ☆☆☆☆" href="#q2-name-some-of-the-events-fired-by-streams--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Each type of Stream is an <strong>EventEmitter</strong> instance and throws several events at different instance of times. For example, some of the commonly used events are:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>data</strong> - This event is fired when there is data is available to read.</li>
<li><strong>end</strong> - This event is fired when there is no more data to read.</li>
<li><strong>error</strong> - This event is fired when there is any error receiving or writing data.</li>
<li><strong>finish</strong> - This event is fired when all data has been flushed to underlying system</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q3: What is the purpose of __filename variable? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q3-what-is-the-purpose-of-__filename-variable--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q3: What is the purpose of __filename variable? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q3-what-is-the-purpose-of-__filename-variable--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The <code>__filename</code> represents the filename of the code being executed. This is the resolved absolute path of this code file. For a main program this is not necessarily the same filename used in the command line. The value inside a module is the path to that module file.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>tutorialspoint.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q4: How can you listen on port 80 with Node? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q4-how-can-you-listen-on-port-80-with-node--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q4: How can you listen on port 80 with Node? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q4-how-can-you-listen-on-port-80-with-node--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Run the application on any port above 1024, then put a reverse proxy like <a href="http://nginx.org/" rel="nofollow">nginx</a> in front of it.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q5: What tools can be used to assure consistent code style? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q5-what-tools-can-be-used-to-assure-consistent-code-style--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q5: What tools can be used to assure consistent code style? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q5-what-tools-can-be-used-to-assure-consistent-code-style--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
You have plenty of options to do so:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><a href="http://jslint.com/" rel="nofollow">JSLint</a> by Douglas Crockford</li>
<li><a href="http://jshint.com/" rel="nofollow">JSHint</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eslint.org/" rel="nofollow">ESLint</a></li>
<li><a href="http://jscs.info/" rel="nofollow">JSCS</a></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">These tools are really helpful when developing code in teams, to enforce a given style guide and to catch common errors using static analysis.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q6: What's a stub? Name a use case. ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q6-whats-a-stub-name-a-use-case--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q6: What's a stub? Name a use case. ☆☆☆☆" href="#q6-whats-a-stub-name-a-use-case--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Stubs</strong> are functions/programs that simulate the behaviours of components/modules. Stubs provide canned answers to function calls made during test cases. Also, you can assert on with what these stubs were called.</p>
<p dir="auto">A use-case can be a file read, when you do not want to read an actual file:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">fs</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'fs'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">readFileStub</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">sinon</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">stub</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">fs</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">'readFile'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">path</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">cb</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">cb</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">null</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">'filecontent'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-en">expect</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">readFileStub</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">to</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">be</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">called</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">readFileStub</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">restore</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>blog.risingstack.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q7: Does Node.js support multi-core platforms? And is it capable of utilizing all the cores? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q7-does-nodejs-support-multi-core-platforms-and-is-it-capable-of-utilizing-all-the-cores--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q7: Does Node.js support multi-core platforms? And is it capable of utilizing all the cores? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q7-does-nodejs-support-multi-core-platforms-and-is-it-capable-of-utilizing-all-the-cores--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes, Node.js would run on a multi-core system without any issue. But it is by default a single-threaded application, so it can’t completely utilize the multi-core system.</p>
<p dir="auto">However, Node.js can facilitate deployment on multi-core systems where it does use the additional hardware. It packages with a Cluster module which is capable of starting multiple Node.js worker processes that will share the same port.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q8: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q8-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q8: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q8-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes, it’s true that Node.js processes all requests on a single thread. But it’s just a part of the theory behind Node.js design. In fact, more than the single thread mechanism, it makes use of events and callbacks to handle a large no. of requests asynchronously.</p>
<p dir="auto">Moreover, Node.js has an optimized design which utilizes both JavaScript and C++ to guarantee maximum performance. JavaScript executes at the server-side by Google Chrome v8 engine. And the C++ lib UV library takes care of the non-sequential I/O via background workers.</p>
<p dir="auto">To explain it practically, let’s assume there are 100s of requests lined up in Node.js queue. As per design, the main thread of Node.js event loop will receive all of them and forwards to background workers for execution. Once the workers finish processing requests, the registered callbacks get notified on event loop thread to pass the result back to the user.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q9: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q9-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q9: Is Node.js entirely based on a single-thread? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q9-is-nodejs-entirely-based-on-a-single-thread--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes, it’s true that Node.js processes all requests on a single thread. But it’s just a part of the theory behind Node.js design. In fact, more than the single thread mechanism, it makes use of events and callbacks to handle a large no. of requests asynchronously.</p>
<p dir="auto">Moreover, Node.js has an optimized design which utilizes both JavaScript and C++ to guarantee maximum performance. JavaScript executes at the server-side by Google Chrome v8 engine. And the C++ lib UV library takes care of the non-sequential I/O via background workers.</p>
<p dir="auto">To explain it practically, let’s assume there are 100s of requests lined up in Node.js queue. As per design, the main thread of Node.js event loop will receive all of them and forwards to background workers for execution. Once the workers finish processing requests, the registered callbacks get notified on event loop thread to pass the result back to the user.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q10: When to not use Node.js? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q10-when-to-not-use-nodejs--1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q10: When to not use Node.js? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q10-when-to-not-use-nodejs--1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
We can use Node.js for a variety of applications. But it is a single threaded framework, so we should not use it for cases where the application requires long processing time. If the server is doing some calculation, it won’t be able to process any other requests. Hence, Node.js is best when processing needs less dedicated CPU time.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>techbeamers.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q11: Why to use Buffers instead of binary strings to handle binary data ? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q11-why-to-use-buffers-instead-of-binary-strings-to-handle-binary-data---1" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q11: Why to use Buffers instead of binary strings to handle binary data ? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q11-why-to-use-buffers-instead-of-binary-strings-to-handle-binary-data---1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Pure JavaScript does not able to handle straight binary data very well. Since Node.js servers have to deal with TCP streams for reading and writing of data, binary strings will become problematic to work with as it is very slow and has a tendency to break. That's why it is always advisable to use Buffers instead of binary strings to handle binary data.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codingdefined.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q12: How to gracefully Shutdown Node.js Server? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q12-how-to-gracefully-shutdown-nodejs-server-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q12: How to gracefully Shutdown Node.js Server? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q12-how-to-gracefully-shutdown-nodejs-server-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
We can gracefully shutdown Node.js server by using the generic signal called SIGTERM or SIGINT which is used for program termination. We need to call SIGTERM or SIGINT which will terminate the program and clean up the resources utilized by the program.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codingdefined.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q13: What are the timing features of Node.js? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q13-what-are-the-timing-features-of-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q13: What are the timing features of Node.js? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q13-what-are-the-timing-features-of-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The Timers module in Node.js contains functions that execute code after a set period of time.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>setTimeout/clearTimeout</strong> - can be used to schedule code execution after a designated amount of milliseconds</li>
<li><strong>setInterval/clearInterval</strong> - can be used to execute a block of code multiple times</li>
<li><strong>setImmediate/clearImmediate</strong> - will execute code at the end of the current event loop cycle</li>
<li><strong>process.nextTick</strong> - used to schedule a callback function to be invoked in the next iteration of the Event Loop</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">cb</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Processed in next iteration'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-s1">process</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">nextTick</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">cb</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Processed in the first iteration'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Output:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-v">Processed</span> <span class="pl-k">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">the</span> <span class="pl-s1">first</span> <span class="pl-s1">iteration</span>
<span class="pl-v">Processed</span> <span class="pl-k">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">next</span> <span class="pl-s1">iteration</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/jimuyouyou</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q14: Explain usage of NODE_ENV ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q14-explain-usage-of-node_env-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q14: Explain usage of NODE_ENV ☆☆☆☆" href="#q14-explain-usage-of-node_env-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Node encourages the convention of using a variable called NODE_ENV to flag whether we’re in production right now. This determination allows components to provide better diagnostics during development, for example by disabling caching or emitting verbose log statements. Setting NODE_ENV to production makes your application 3 times faster.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell" dir="auto"><pre>// Setting environment variables <span class="pl-k">in</span> bash before starting the node process
$ NODE_ENV=development
$ node

// Reading the environment variable using code
<span class="pl-k">if</span> (process.env.NODE_ENV === “production”)
useCaching = <span class="pl-c1">true</span><span class="pl-k">;</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/i0natan/nodebestpractices</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q15: What is LTS releases of Node.js why should you care? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q15-what-is-lts-releases-of-nodejs-why-should-you-care-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q15: What is LTS releases of Node.js why should you care? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q15-what-is-lts-releases-of-nodejs-why-should-you-care-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
An <strong>LTS(Long Term Support)</strong> version of Node.js receives all the critical bug fixes, security updates and performance improvements.</p>
<p dir="auto">LTS versions of Node.js are supported for at least 18 months and are indicated by even version numbers (e.g. 4, 6, 8). They're best for production since the LTS release line is focussed on stability and security, whereas the <em>Current</em> release line has a shorter lifespan and more frequent updates to the code. Changes to LTS versions are limited to bug fixes for stability, security updates, possible npm updates, documentation updates and certain performance improvements that can be demonstrated to not break existing applications.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/i0natan/nodebestpractices</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q16: Provide some example of config file separation for dev and prod environments ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q16-provide-some-example-of-config-file-separation-for-dev-and-prod-environments-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q16: Provide some example of config file separation for dev and prod environments ☆☆☆☆" href="#q16-provide-some-example-of-config-file-separation-for-dev-and-prod-environments-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
A perfect and flawless configuration setup should ensure:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>keys can be read from file AND from environment variable</li>
<li>secrets are kept outside committed code</li>
<li>config is hierarchical for easier findability</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Consider the following config file:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">config</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">production</span>: <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">mongo</span> : <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
      <span class="pl-c1">billing</span>: <span class="pl-s">'****'</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
  <span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">default</span>: <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-c1">mongo</span> : <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
      <span class="pl-c1">billing</span>: <span class="pl-s">'****'</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
  <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-s1">exports</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">get</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">get</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">env</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">config</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s1">env</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span> <span class="pl-c1">||</span> <span class="pl-s1">config</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">default</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto">And it's usage:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">config</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'./config/config.js'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">get</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">process</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">env</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">NODE_ENV</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">dbconn</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">mongoose</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">createConnection</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">config</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">mongo</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">billing</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/i0natan/nodebestpractices</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q17: How would you handle errors for async code in Node.js? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q17-how-would-you-handle-errors-for-async-code-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q17: How would you handle errors for async code in Node.js? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q17-how-would-you-handle-errors-for-async-code-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Handling async errors in callback style (error-first approach) is probably the fastest way to hell (a.k.a the pyramid of doom). It's better to use a reputable promise library or async-await instead which enables a much more compact and familiar code syntax like try-catch.</p>
<p dir="auto">Consider promises to catch errors:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-en">doWork</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
 <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">doWork</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
 <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">doOtherWork</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
 <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">result</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">doWork</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
 <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">catch</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">error</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-k">throw</span> <span class="pl-s1">error</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
 <span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">verify</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">or using async/await:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">async</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">check</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">req</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">res</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">try</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">someOtherFunction</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
        <span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">b</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">somethingElseFunction</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
        <span class="pl-s1">res</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">send</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"result"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span> <span class="pl-k">catch</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">error</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-s1">res</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">send</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">error</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">stack</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>github.com/i0natan/nodebestpractices</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q18: What's the difference between dependencies, devDependencies and peerDependencies in npm package.json file? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q18-whats-the-difference-between-dependencies-devdependencies-and-peerdependencies-in-npm-packagejson-file-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q18: What's the difference between dependencies, devDependencies and peerDependencies in npm package.json file? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q18-whats-the-difference-between-dependencies-devdependencies-and-peerdependencies-in-npm-packagejson-file-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>dependencies</strong> - Dependencies that your project needs to run, like a library that provides functions that you call from your code. They are installed transitively (if A depends on B depends on C, npm install on A will install B and C).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>devDependencies</strong> - Dependencies you only need during development or releasing, like compilers that take your code and compile it into javascript, test frameworks or documentation generators. They are not installed transitively (if A depends on B dev-depends on C, npm install on A will install B only).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>peerDependencies</strong> - Dependencies that your project hooks into, or modifies, in the parent project, usually a plugin for some other library or tool. It is just intended to be a check, making sure that the parent project (project that will depend on your project) has a dependency on the project you hook into. So if you make a plugin C that adds functionality to library B, then someone making a project A will need to have a dependency on B if they have a dependency on C. They are not installed (unless npm &lt; 3), they are only checked for.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q19: How do you convert an existing callback API to promises? ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q19-how-do-you-convert-an-existing-callback-api-to-promises-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q19: How do you convert an existing callback API to promises? ☆☆☆☆" href="#q19-how-do-you-convert-an-existing-callback-api-to-promises-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Details:</strong>
How to convert this callback code to Promise? Provide some examples.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">divisionAPI</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">number</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">divider</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">successCallback</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">errorCallback</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">divider</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">errorCallback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Division by zero"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">)</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">successCallback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span> <span class="pl-s1">number</span> <span class="pl-c1">/</span> <span class="pl-s1">divider</span> <span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">divisionAPI</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">number</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">divider</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Promise</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">fulfilled</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">rejected</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">divider</span> <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
            <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">rejected</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"Division by zero"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
        <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
        <span class="pl-s1">fulfilled</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">number</span> <span class="pl-c1">/</span> <span class="pl-s1">divider</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-c">// Promise can be used with together async\await in ES7 to make the program flow wait for a fullfiled result</span>
<span class="pl-k">async</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">foo</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">result</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">divisionAPI</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span> <span class="pl-c">// awaits for a fulfilled result!</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">result</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-c">// Another usage with the same code by using .then() method</span>
<span class="pl-en">divisionAPI</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">result</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">result</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto">Node.js 8.0.0 includes a new <code>util.promisify()</code> API that allows standard Node.js callback style APIs to be wrapped in a function that returns a Promise.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">fs</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'fs'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">util</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'util'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-s1">readfile</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">util</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">promisify</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">fs</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">readFile</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-s1">readfile</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'/some/file'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">data</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-c">/** ... **/</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">catch</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-c1">=&gt;</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-c">/** ... **/</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>stackoverflow.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q20: What are async functions in Node? Provide some examples. ☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q20-what-are-async-functions-in-node-provide-some-examples-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q20: What are async functions in Node? Provide some examples. ☆☆☆☆" href="#q20-what-are-async-functions-in-node-provide-some-examples-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
With the release of Node.js 8, the long awaited async functions have landed in Node.js as well. ES 2017 introduced Asynchronous functions. Async functions are essentially a cleaner way to work with asynchronous code in JavaScript.</p>
<p dir="auto">Async/Await is:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>The newest way to write asynchronous code in JavaScript.</li>
<li>It is non blocking (just like promises and callbacks).</li>
<li>Async/Await was created to simplify the process of working with and writing chained promises.</li>
<li>Async functions return a Promise. If the function throws an error, the Promise will be rejected. If the function returns a value, the Promise will be resolved.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Async functions</strong> can make use of the <code>await</code> expression. This will pause the async function and wait for the <em>Promise</em> to resolve prior to moving on.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q1: Consider following code snippet ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q1-consider-following-code-snippet-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q1: Consider following code snippet ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q1-consider-following-code-snippet-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Details:</strong>
Consider following code snippet:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">time</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"loop"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">i</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span> <span class="pl-s1">i</span> <span class="pl-c1">&lt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">1000000</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span> <span class="pl-s1">i</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-c">// Do nothing</span>
  <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">timeEnd</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"loop"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The time required to run this code in Google Chrome is considerably more than the time required to run it in Node.js Explain why this is so, even though both use the v8 JavaScript Engine.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Within a web browser such as Chrome, declaring the variable <code>i</code> outside of any function’s scope makes it global and therefore binds it as a property of the <code>window</code> object. As a result, running this code in a web browser requires repeatedly resolving the property <code>i</code> within the heavily populated <code>window</code> namespace in each iteration of the <code>for</code> loop.</p>
<p dir="auto">In Node.js, however, declaring any variable outside of any function’s scope binds it only to the module’s own scope (not the <code>window</code> object) which therefore makes it much easier and faster to resolve.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>toptal.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q2: Can Node.js use other engines than V8? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q2-can-nodejs-use-other-engines-than-v8-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q2: Can Node.js use other engines than V8? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q2-can-nodejs-use-other-engines-than-v8-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Yes. Microsoft Chakra is another JavaScript engine which can be used with Node.js. It’s not officially declared yet.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codeforgeek.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q3: How would you scale Node application? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q3-how-would-you-scale-node-application-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q3: How would you scale Node application? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q3-how-would-you-scale-node-application-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
We can scale Node application in following ways:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>cloning using <em>Cluster</em> module.</li>
<li>decomposing the application into smaller services – i.e micro services.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codeforgeek.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q4: What is the difference between process.nextTick() and setImmediate() ? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q4-what-is-the-difference-between-processnexttick-and-setimmediate--" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q4: What is the difference between process.nextTick() and setImmediate() ? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q4-what-is-the-difference-between-processnexttick-and-setimmediate--"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
The difference between <code>process.nextTick()</code> and <code>setImmediate()</code> is that <code>process.nextTick()</code> defers the execution of an action till the next pass around the event loop or it simply calls the callback function once the ongoing execution of the event loop is finished whereas <code>setImmediate()</code> executes a callback on the next cycle of the event loop and it gives back to the event loop for executing any I/O operations.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codingdefined.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q5: How to solve "Process out of Memory Exception" in Node.js ? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q5-how-to-solve-process-out-of-memory-exception-in-nodejs--" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q5: How to solve &quot;Process out of Memory Exception&quot; in Node.js ? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q5-how-to-solve-process-out-of-memory-exception-in-nodejs--"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
To solve the process out of memory exception in Node.js we need to increase the <code>max-old-space-size</code>. By default the max size of max-old-space-size is 512 mb which you can increase by the command:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell" dir="auto"><pre>node --max-old-space-size=1024 file.js</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>codingdefined.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q6: Explain what is Reactor Pattern in Node.js? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q6-explain-what-is-reactor-pattern-in-nodejs-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q6: Explain what is Reactor Pattern in Node.js? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q6-explain-what-is-reactor-pattern-in-nodejs-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
<strong>Reactor Pattern</strong> is an idea of non-blocking I/O operations in Node.js. This pattern provides a handler(in case of Node.js, a <em>callback function</em>) that is associated with each I/O operation. When an I/O request is generated, it is submitted to a <em>demultiplexer</em>.</p>
<p dir="auto">This <em>demultiplexer</em> is a notification interface that is used to handle concurrency in non-blocking I/O mode and collects every request in form of an event and queues each event in a queue. Thus, the demultiplexer provides the <em>Event Queue</em>.</p>
<p dir="auto">At the same time, there is an Event Loop which iterates over the items in the Event Queue. Every event has a callback function associated with it, and that callback function is invoked when the Event Loop iterates.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>hackernoon.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q7: Explain some Error Handling approaches in Node.js you know about. Which one will you use? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q7-explain-some-error-handling-approaches-in-nodejs-you-know-about-which-one-will-you-use-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q7: Explain some Error Handling approaches in Node.js you know about. Which one will you use? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q7-explain-some-error-handling-approaches-in-nodejs-you-know-about-which-one-will-you-use-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Error handling in an asynchronous language works in a unique way and presents many challenges, some unexpected. There are four main error handling patterns in node:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Error return value</strong> - doesn't work asynchronously</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">validateObject</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">obj</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">typeof</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">!==</span> <span class="pl-s">'object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Invalid object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Error throwing</strong> - well-establish pattern, in which a function does its thing and if an error situation arises, it simply bails out throwing an error. Can leave you in an unstable state. It requires extra work to catch them. Also wrapping the async calls in try/catch won't help because the errors happen asynchronously. To fix this, we need <em>domains</em>. Domains provide an asynchronous try...catch.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">validateObject</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">obj</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">typeof</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">!==</span> <span class="pl-s">'object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">throw</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Invalid object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">try</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-en">validateObject</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'123'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-k">catch</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Thrown: '</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">message</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>

<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Error callback</strong> - returning an error via a callback is the most common error handling pattern in Node.js. Handling error callbacks can become a mess (callback hell or the pyramid of doom).</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">validateObject</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">obj</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">typeof</span> <span class="pl-s1">obj</span> <span class="pl-c1">!==</span> <span class="pl-s">'object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
        <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Invalid object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
    <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-en">validateObject</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'123'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Callback: '</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">message</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Error emitting</strong> - when emitting errors, the errors are broadcast to any interested subscribers and handled within the same process tick, in the order subscribed.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-v">Events</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'events'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">emitter</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Events</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">EventEmitter</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-en">validateObject</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">a</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">typeof</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">!==</span> <span class="pl-s">'object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-s1">emitter</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">emit</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'error'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Invalid object'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-s1">emitter</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">on</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'error'</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'Emitted: '</span> <span class="pl-c1">+</span> <span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">message</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-en">validateObject</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'123'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Promises</strong> for async error handling</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-en">doWork</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">doWork</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">doError</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">doWork</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">catch</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">errorHandler</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">then</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">verify</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Try...catch with async/await</strong> - ES7 Async/await allows us as developers to write asynchronous JS code that look synchronous.</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">async</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">f</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>

<span class="pl-k">try</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">let</span> <span class="pl-s1">response</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">fetch</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'http://no-such-url'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span> <span class="pl-k">catch</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-en">alert</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span> <span class="pl-c">// TypeError: failed to fetch</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>

<span class="pl-en">f</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>

<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Await-to-js lib</strong> - async/await without try-catch blocks in Javascript</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">to</span> <span class="pl-k">from</span> <span class="pl-s">'await-to-js'</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">async</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span><span class="pl-s1">quote</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">await</span> <span class="pl-en">to</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-en">getQuote</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

    <span class="pl-k">if</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">err</span> <span class="pl-c1">||</span> <span class="pl-c1">!</span><span class="pl-s1">quote</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-v">Error</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'No Quote found'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos"></span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

    <span class="pl-s1">callback</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">null</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span><span class="pl-s1">quote</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>

<p dir="auto"><strong>Source:</strong> <em>gist.github.com</em></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 class="heading-element" dir="auto">Q8: Why should you separate Express 'app' and 'server'? ☆☆☆☆☆</h3><a id="user-content-q8-why-should-you-separate-express-app-and-server-" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Q8: Why should you separate Express 'app' and 'server'? ☆☆☆☆☆" href="#q8-why-should-you-separate-express-app-and-server-"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Answer:</strong>
Keeping the API declaration separated from the network related configuration (port, protocol, etc) allows testing the API in-process, without performing network calls, with all the benefits that it brings to the table: fast testing execution and getting coverage metrics of the code. It also allows deploying the same API under flexible and different network conditions. Bonus: better separation of concerns and cleaner code.</p>
<p dir="auto">API declaration, should reside in app.js:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">app</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">express</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">app</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">use</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">bodyParser</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">json</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">app</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">use</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"/api/events"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">events</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">API</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-s1">app</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">use</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"/api/forms"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s1">forms</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Server network declaration, should reside in /bin/www:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js" dir="auto"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">app</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'../app'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">http</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">require</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">'http'</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
